No reliance on textbooks, 2. No reliance on teachers, 3. No reliance on training, the words are mostly pertinent, and the listeners are moved. A Major Event in Cultural History 219

Contract for Printing the Siku Quanshu in Facsimile

Each set will be bound into 1,500 volumes.

A maximum of 1,500 sets will be printed.

This newspaper has repeatedly reported that the National Government's plan to print unpublished rare manuscripts from the Siku Quanshu in facsimile has been approved by the Executive Yuan, and that Chiang Fu-tsung, Director of the Preparatory Office of the Central Library, was specially appointed by the Ministry of Education to come to Shanghai and sign a formal contract with the Commercial Press for printing and distribution. According to Wang Yun-wu, General Manager of the Press, in a formal statement to a reporter from the New Voice Society, the reports in the newspapers today regarding this matter differ somewhat from the facts. A reporter visited yesterday and was received by Mr. Hsu Lien-seng, a staff member of the Press. What was reported was not based on my conversation. In fact, the number of copies to be printed will be determined after considering the number of pre-orders. The amount of paper to be used is related to the number of books printed, so it is difficult to estimate at this time. As for the number of sets to be donated to the Central Library, it will be guaranteed to be one-tenth of the actual number printed. The original text of the contract has been obtained and is disclosed below:

Contract between the National Central Library Preparatory Office and the Shanghai Commercial Press. Both parties agree to the following terms and conditions:

Article 1: The Ministry of Education commissions the National Central Library Preparatory Office (hereinafter referred to as "the Library") to enter into a contract with the Shanghai Commercial Press (hereinafter referred to as "the Press") to photographically reproduce and publish the unpublished rare woodblock editions from the Wen Yuan Ge Siku Quanshu in a small 16mo format.

Article 2: The photographic reproduction of the unpublished rare manuscripts shall be limited to 90,000 pages, with each set bound into approximately 1,500 volumes in Chinese binding.

Article 3: For the sake of careful preservation, the Ministry of Education shall petition the Executive Yuan for special permission to allow the Library to send personnel to accompany the Press to the Palace Museum (Shanghai storage location) for photographing the rare manuscripts intended for printing.

Article 4: During the photographing process, the Palace Museum, together with the Library, shall send personnel to check and hand over the books to be photographed by the Press each day. Once the photographing is completed each day, the Press shall return the books immediately. The Press shall only be relieved of responsibility after the Palace Museum and the Library have sent personnel to the site to verify the count without error.

Article 5: The photographing time shall not exceed six months.

Article 6: All printing costs shall be borne by the Press. The Library shall not be responsible for any profits or losses.

Article 7: The complete set of books shall be published within two years from the date of photographing, without any extension on the grounds of delay. The first year shall be for pre-sales and plate-making. The books due to the Library shall be delivered in two installments during the second year.

Article 8: The paper used shall be Jiangnan Maobian paper produced by the Jiangnan Paper Mill.

Article 9: The selling price shall be determined by the Press based on the cost of labor and materials.

Article 10: The number of copies printed shall be determined by the Press. One-tenth of the printed number shall be donated to the Library. If the number of copies printed is less than 300, at least 30 copies shall still be donated. The maximum number of copies to be photographically reproduced shall be 1,500.

Article 11: The Press shall not extract and print separate single volumes from the complete set. Each set must be stamped by the Library before it can be sold. However, in the event of unavoidable accidents and not due to the fault of the Press, and the photographing cannot be completed, the Press may request the Ministry of Education to allow it to print the photographed books as single volumes and sell them directly, and shall still donate to the Library in accordance with the provisions of Article 10.

Article 12: The copyright of the entire publication shall belong to the Library, which entrusts the Press to print and distribute it.

Article 13: Special care should be taken during the photographing process to avoid soiling or damaging the manuscripts. If any damage occurs, the Press shall compensate by copying the damaged page in the same format and returning the damaged original page.

Article 14: This contract grants the Press the right to print this book for one edition only. If a reprint is necessary, both parties shall negotiate and enter into a separate contract.

Article 15: This contract is made in duplicate, one copy to be submitted by the Library to the Ministry of Education, and one copy to be retained by the Press.

June 17, 1933

Signed: National Central Library Preparatory Office Shanghai Commercial Press

Announced by the Municipal Board of Education

Service Regulations for Teachers and Staff of People's Schools 220

The Second People's School has been established.

The "One Yuan Per Month for Education" campaign initiated by the Shanghai Municipal Board of Education is being carried out with great effort. In addition to the First People's School, which has already been opened, the Second People's School has also been established. The location is inside the Puyu Primary School in Sanminfang, Puyu East Road.

Chen Rong-fa has been appointed as the principal. The area nearby is mostly inhabited by common people, with illiteracy rates estimated at 95%. The establishment of this school will greatly benefit society. It is reported that the school will open next week. The following are the regulations for the appointment, dismissal, and service of teachers and staff of the People's Schools as announced by the Board:

Article 1: The principal of the Municipal Board of Education People's School is appointed by the Municipal Board of Education, and the teachers and staff are hired by the principal.

Article 2: The qualifications of the principals and teachers of each school shall meet the standards for primary school principals and teachers.

Article 3: The term of office for the principals and teachers of each school shall be four months.

Article 4: If any principal or teacher violates the Three People's Principles of the Chinese Kuomintang, the educational laws and regulations of the National Government, the People's School regulations set by the Shanghai Municipal Board of Education, or if their teaching is ineffective or their performance is poor, the Municipal Board of Education may, after investigation and confirmation, terminate their employment at any time.

Article 5: The duties of the principals and teachers of the Municipal Board of Education People's Schools are as follows:

(A) Principal: (1) Implement people's education based on the Three People's Principles; (2) Handle all internal and external affairs; (3) Consult with the Municipal Board of Education regarding the appointment and dismissal of teachers; (4) Evaluate the performance of teachers; (5) Supervise and guide teachers in handling all matters related to students; (6) Supervise and assist in the education of elderly illiterate people nearby, and encourage them to enroll in school, investigate social occupational conditions, and determine teaching subjects; (7) Manage all school funds; (8) Supervise teachers in compiling various forms and registers; (9) Examine student performance.

(B) Teachers: (1) Assist the principal in handling school affairs, teaching affairs, and all other matters; (2) Collect and edit teaching materials; (3) Contact student families and their service organizations; (4) Investigate student absences and reasons for withdrawal; (5) Fill out various forms and registers; (6) Be responsible for student training; (7) Attend discussion meetings organized by the Municipal Board of Education.

Article 6: If the principal needs to take leave for three days or more, they must formally appoint a substitute and submit a request to the Municipal Board of Education for approval. Teachers taking leave must report to the principal and appoint a substitute.

Article 7: The principal should also teach courses, or teachers should be self-appointed by the principal.

Article 8: These regulations shall be implemented after being passed by the Municipal Board of Education meeting.

Essays

Dumping 232

— Lily

In the eyes of foreigners, Chinese people are associated with "bound feet," "queues," "opium smoking," "spitting," "farting," and "unpatriotic" behavior, with nothing commendable. The only "different" and "pleasing" trait is the "love for foreign goods."

"High-class Chinese" love "Western goods," while those below them, from "boycott overseas" to "coolies," love "Eastern goods" or use both "Eastern goods" and "Western goods." Although the products bear the phrase "Made in China" in foreign languages, indicating a "foreign touch," the upper, middle, and lower classes generally think, "Oh, domestic goods, humph!"

Chinese people are truly "blessed like the East Sea." These years, they are suffering from "expensive gold and cheap silver," unable to afford foreign goods. Coincidentally, foreigners are experiencing a "surplus of production," and their eyes are set on the "foreign-loving" Chinese people, "selling lamb at the price of dog meat," and "dumping at any cost."

"Russian goods" want to squeeze out "Western goods," "Eastern goods" want to overthrow "Russian goods," and "Western goods" want to drive away "Eastern goods." You are having a "clearance sale of inventory," I am "treating customers preferentially with a buy-one-get-one-free offer," and he is having a "cheap sale of good goods with extra gifts." "Since I have to buy it anyway, might as well get it cheap." "When the snipe and clam fight, the fisherman benefits." Foreigners are ultimately benefiting because of the reckless "dumping," China "can reduce the outflow of several million yuan each year."

"The Tianjin-Beijing war has ended." The long "national crisis" is beginning to show a glimmer of hope. We, the masters of the Republic of China who tremble with fear of becoming "slaves of a conquered nation," can temporarily stop "lying on firewood (lying high and drawing salary is an exception) for several years." Since "resisting foreign aggression" has "come to an end," "internal peace" has also "greatly improved." "Harmony is in the air," perhaps "the world will be at peace" soon, and we should also "enjoy ourselves in time," without having to "scrimp and save" anymore, busy with "comforting" here and "donating" there.

How to "enjoy ourselves in time?" To be frank, see through things, "spend money today if you have it," buy some food you haven't eaten, buy some clothes you haven't worn, buy some things you haven't used.

"Western goods," "Eastern goods," and "Russian goods" are all having "massive sales." Everything to eat, wear, and use is available. In order to "reduce the outflow of several million yuan each year," from "high-class Chinese" to "boycott overseas" to "coolies," everyone should stand at attention, raise their hands, and welcome them.

The Lives of Traveling Performers 233

— Tu Nan

Traveling performers are the kind who make a living with art. Among them, there are many young girls with both beauty and talent, performing amazing stunts. However, life in such troupes is very painful. The troupe leader only cares about winning the audience's appreciation and earning more rewards, so they spur them on to perform hard. Even if they have some pain or discomfort, they are not allowed to rest. Although the troupe leader's methods are cruel, there is no choice given the necessity of making a living. Sometimes, if they are unlucky, local bullies will force them to be their concubines. The troupe, relying on them as money trees, would never agree. But the bullies' evil power is very strong, and they find various ways to ruin them. The troupe cannot stand their ground and has no choice but to wander elsewhere.

Regarding traveling performances, there is also a more romantic and meaningful thing. A young man from a family of scholars and etiquette fell in love with a performing girl, and their love burned like fire. In the era of the shackles of the old moral teachings, he was actually able to break through the boundaries of social class, obtain the consent of his parents, break off his engagement with his betrothed wife, and resolutely marry this performing girl as his wife. Not only did he not despise her profession, but he also encouraged her to help him improve his art into a noble and educational entertainment.

These days, the new film "The Road to Fitness" by the Star Film Company is being shown at the New Light Grand Theater. It takes the theme of traveling performance. Ms. Xu Qin-fang plays the performing girl, and her performance is lively and can fully reveal the estimation of a traveling wanderer. This film, whether in terms of consciousness or technique, is worth seeing.

Anecdotes of Wang Yin-cai 234

— Qing Qu

Wang Yin-cai passed away last week at his home in Shuangqiao, Nanxiang. It is said that when the coffin was being prepared, there was a heavy thunderstorm. The body, which was originally stout, had a belly as large as a five-stone gourd, and could not be

enclosed. Later, the craftsman was instructed to hollow out an inch and a half from the bottom of the coffin before it could be sealed. Alas, this is indeed strange!

Wang initially took education as his responsibility. For thirty years, he was quite well-known in Shanghai, especially in the local area. Whenever he lectured, he would say: "I am a bat." This is because he was born in Jiading, but he entered the Shanghai register for the boy's exam. Four years ago, with the qualification of a teacher, he became the head of Wu County. At that time, Shen Xin-gong and Gu Yin-ting from my county, and others, all boarded sedan chairs to hold official posts and entered the political world. Wang's term of office was longer than Gu Shen's in Wujin and Nanhui. When he resigned, it was said that it was due to the collection of the "power rice" that he was hit by the farmers' association and left. He described that in the Su County government office, he had no free time all day long and suffered a lot. He often used calligraphy and painting to entertain himself. One day, someone brought a large ancient painting, and after examining it for a long time, he took out 800 gold to pay for it. Before long, he knew it was a fake, but it was too late. The money he spent on such things was a large portion of his official wealth.

When he was young, he occasionally uttered obscene words. His father, Gu Sheng, lightly tapped his head with the mouth of a smoking pipe and said, "What are you saying?" His father forbade hitting the head when teaching children, but only allowed slapping the palm and the leg, and did not allow slapping the palm. Using the pipe mouth was strict but contained love. Therefore, Wang had the deepest understanding of teaching methods from his father's teachings. Gu Sheng once recited Wu Meicun's poem: "Do you not see the white waves stirring the sky, a single leaf is in danger. Putting away the reeds, I am still afraid the boat will be slow. People in the world have endless troubles, better to tell the fishing old man of the rivers and lakes," to warn his three sons, but he did not expect that Wang would also enter the political sea for a time. When the bad news reached Shanghai this time, his beloved concubine learned of it and went to Xiang, but was discovered by the wife and was not allowed to enter the door. Later,

a relative paved the way for her, and she was able to weep and bow before the coffin in the name of a female disciple.

Ban left and led Zhao Ziqiang in. He was very polite, rushing in through the door and shaking hands with Gan Erye several times. He moved a chair and asked him to sit down, smiling and saying, "For people like us who are staying in a guild hall, it's already very good to have friends visit. How dare we mention the word 'presumptuous'?" As he spoke, he seemed to remember something and immediately picked up two books to cover something on the table. Before the books were completely down, Zhao Ziqiang had already clearly seen that there was a pawn ticket on the table with two stacks of silver dollars on top. Gan Ji Zhi put the books down to cover the pawn ticket, pretending to be very casual. From this, it was clear that he desperately wanted to hide his poverty. Looking around the room, besides two square stools and two semi-old trunks stacked by the bedside, there were no other valuable items. The bed was basically just a wooden frame. There was no tablecloth on the square table, just a thick layer of newspapers. But there were many books piled up in a mess. From this, one could also see how poor he was. This completely dispelled Zhao Ziqiang's original idea that he had been promoted. So he smiled at him and said, "My coming today is indeed a bit presumptuous, but I have some business to discuss." Ji Zhi smiled and said, "Company Commander Zhao, just tell me what you want." As he spoke, he picked up the old teapot from the corner of the table, poured a cup of plain boiled water, and placed it in front of Zhao Ziqiang. He smiled and said, "I'm really sorry. When you come to a place like mine, there's not even tea or cigarettes." Zhao Ziqiang smiled and said, "Please don't be so polite. If I were being polite, I wouldn't have come so presumptuously. I've already told the old lady Yang what you asked me to convey last time. What did she say?" As he spoke, he watched Ji Zhi's face. Ji Zhi smiled and said, "I guessed they wouldn't say anything." Zhao Ziqiang said, "Isn't Mr. Gan living with your brother in Haidian? Why did you move into the city alone? Do you have a good job?" (107)

Miscellaneous Talk

Idle Chat About Red Beans (Part 1) 237

— Yu Youqing

Red beans, also known as love seeds, are produced in Lingnan. They are woody vines, with trunks more than ten feet tall. The leaves are pinnately compound, and they bloom with small flowers in autumn. The corolla is butterfly-shaped, white or light red. The fruit forms pods, as large as peas, slightly flat, and bright red, sometimes half red and half black. Legend has it that someone died on the border, and his wife missed him so much that she cried under a tree and died. Hence the name. Since the Tang Dynasty, poets have often praised them.

Guangdong New Language: The wood grain of the love seed is similar to that of the locust tree. Large ones, when sawn diagonally, have fine floral patterns, also called chicken wing wood, because their grain resembles it.

Tao Hongjing’s Brief Talk on Red Beans: Red beans are also called love seeds, their color is red, moist and dripping. The flowers are like catalpa, the pods are small like locust horns, and they bear fruit once every few years. Wang Wei of the Tang Dynasty has a poem entitled "Acacia": "Red beans grow in the southern country, How many branches will sprout in the spring? I hope you pick them abundantly, This thing evokes the most yearning." In the Tang Dynasty, this thing was already regarded as a fine product.

Wen Tingyun’s "New Tune, Willow Branches": "Exquisite dice inlaid with red beans, Do you know how deep is the yearning that penetrates the bones?" Red bean yearning can penetrate deep into the bones.

Xue Tian’s poem: "Elegant shops pile up red beans, A潇洒courtyard reflects bright green, This scene and this feeling, make people yearn."

Wang Chan Hong's personal poem: "Behind the screen, recording tunes and picking red beans, Under the window, copying books and dyeing green bananas." Where is the individual? Making people think, a finishing touch, the sentence is also well-crafted.

Chen Yunping’s "Spring Returns": "After the swallows return, Seeking red beans under the leaves of yearning," The artistic conception, vividly portrayed.

In Gong Ding'an's collection of Wang Ci Hui’s poems, the words "red bean" often appear, mostly untitled love poems, using the words "red bean" as a decorative element. The Red Bean Mountain Villa, during the Kangxi period of the Qing Dynasty, was the library of Hui Dong in Wuxian. There is a three-volume catalog of the Hundred-Year Hall books. According to Hui, there is a Red Bean Villa, north of the Lengxiang Creek in the southeast of Suzhou City. It was originally Dongchan Temple, with a red bean tree planted by Master White Pigeon, which rotted with age, but new branches sprouted again. Hui Zhouxiang planted a branch in front of the steps and called himself the Master of the Red Bean. Monk Mu Cun painted a picture of the new residence of the Red Bean, as seen in Lang Ji’s hearsay. Therefore, the library is also named Red Bean. Red Bean Villa, the residence of Qian Qianyi, the late Mu Zhai in the Qing Dynasty, is located in Changshu County, also named because of the red bean trees there. Qianyi called himself the Red Bean Elder.

Once, Master White Pigeon of Lichen Temple in Wumen, accidentally picked up a red bean and planted it in the temple, pointing and instructing it: "You should grow quickly, but you must not bloom without reason in the future. There are big and small changes in the world, so the blooming of flowers will be sparse or dense," as seen in Niu Xiu's anthology. The ruins of Dongchan Temple are unknown, but the red bean tree still exists, now belonging to Xu Qizhong's family, and its location is near Fengmen in Suzhou. Master White Pigeon entrusted the changes of the world to the red beans, holding them accountable for their density, the old monk is too ignorant of things. A smile.

Legend has it that there are only three red bean trees in the world, one in Changshu, which is the so-called Red Bean Mountain Villa, one in Suzhou, which is the property of Xu Qizhong's family. One in Wenzhou, there is no record, it cannot be verified, this is what Xu Qizhong said in his Red Bean Trivia. As far as I know, there is also one tree in Gushan, Jiangyin, and one tree in Yongning Village, Shantang, Mudu Town, Suzhou. I have not seen the red bean tree in Gushan, but I saw the red bean tree in Mudu last summer. The tree is tall, but there are not many fruits, and the color is light and less round.

The anthology states: "Once there was a grieving woman who looked forward to her husband's return every day, shedding tears under a tree, her blood dyed the branches, which then formed seeds. This is the origin of the love seed. The poet entrusts things in the poem "Southern Country", which cannot be taken as fact."

Xu Qizhong has a red bean poem: "Holding the parrot grain, three points of jealousy, The heart penetrates the rhinoceros, a little infatuation," Comparing the red bean to the parrot grain, there is the thinking of Yishan's Brocade Zither. Han Yun Yuan Kewen once founded the Red Bean Newspaper with Yu Yifen, but it died after a few issues. The name "Red Bean" makes me feel infinitely nostalgic. Now the literary friends are old, and the clouds have returned. Praising a certain gentleman's poem mourning Yuan, there is a line "A lifetime of business, how many red skirts?", Can Xinling poison wine women, get what they want? I can't help but feel emotional about it. In the past, Han Yun once asked me for a pair of red beans, through the introduction of Jin friend Chen Jun. Now that Han Yun has passed away, I wonder if the pair of red beans are still there?

Hua Dabai obtained a pair of red beans from Zhou Gangzhi of Jiangyin, and there are three Double Red Bean tunes. Now I excerpt a few sentences, saying: "A good name called Red Bean," saying: "Afraid of planting the seeds of yearning," saying: "Double red beans stored in a brocade pouch," saying: "Relying on this to convey yearning." The beans are passed down through people, and people are passed down through words, I am fortunate for the red beans. Gangzhi became a martyr, and Dabai's tomb is also covered with green grass. I heard that Dabai was very lonely after his death, making people lament that literati are often poor.

As the amount of Fujian rice decreases daily, the "Ke Xian" market has also become increasingly sluggish. Yesterday, the supply of Fujian rice completely stopped, and there were no transactions for "Ke Xian" rice. Even "Che Xian", "Du Jian", and "Yang Jian" Ke Xian were weak. The whole market saw only 316 bags of Wuxi coarse rice handled by the Wenzhou and Taizhou merchants, priced at $6.35 per bag. There were no other transactions. "Foreign rice," on the other hand, has become lively. Two batches of Saigon No. 1 new rice have recently arrived in Shanghai, totaling 15,000 bags, all handled by foreign merchants. The asking price is very high, and no sales have been made yet. Local merchants are quite interested. Yesterday, the Zhejiang route saw excellent sales. Wenzhou and Taizhou merchants handled 2,200 bags of small "Jiao" rice, priced at $6.65 per bag. Additionally, 560 bags of Zhongguan large "Jiao" rice were handled by Ningbo and Shaoxing merchants. Due to active demand, the price of small "Jiao" rice has increased by five cents.

Post-Flour and Wheat Market Outlook is Positive 253

The flour market opened this morning with prices initially flat, then trending upwards. As foreign wheat quotations rebounded by about 3-4 cents, the market appeared weak at the open. However, after the second session, prices steadily rose. As floods in various provinces are becoming a reality, people inside and outside the industry are inevitably fearful. Northern merchants are also actively trading, leading to a gradual increase in market activity. By the afternoon opening, all months had resumed their upward trend. Tianjin, Shandong, and local speculators were all actively buying, and rumors of Japanese merchants buying old wheat further fueled sentiment. Prices briefly stabilized after a major factory released its holdings. Looking ahead, if the floods in various provinces do not expand, the rumors should subside, and the market will not see runaway price increases. As a result, June and July contracts rose 2.25 cents compared to the previous day, August and September contracts rose 2.5 cents, October contracts rose 2.25 cents, and November contracts rose 1.5 cents.

The wheat market opened this morning with prices initially flat, then steadily rising. As foreign wheat quotations fell by 3-4 cents, concerns about unfavorable weather and potential floods in various provinces led some speculators to actively buy, and those shorting the market rushed to cover their positions, resulting in a significant price increase. By the afternoon opening, the flour market was also strong, and rumors of Japanese merchants secretly inspecting old wheat caused market anxiety, leading to a sharp rise in prices. However, these events are currently only rumors, and the overall price trend remains uncertain. As a result, July contracts rose 7 cents compared to the previous day, August contracts rose 8 cents, September contracts rose 9 cents, October contracts rose a significant 11 cents, and November contracts rose 10 cents. The current wheat market remains flat for mid-grade and low-grade wheat, while high-grade wheat is slightly active. Wheat from Jiangyan, Huangqiao, and Dongtai is quoted at $3.75, Taizhou and Liuhe wheat at $3.60, Hezhou wheat at $3.68, Wuhu wheat at $3.71, Nanjing wheat at $3.60, Pukou wheat at $3.75 to $3.60, Yangzhou wheat at $3.68, Penglai wheat at $3.50, Zhitang wheat at $3.65, and Kunshan wheat at $3.70 to $3.65, totaling 8,500 bags handled by Fuxin, Fufeng, Shenda, and Huafeng.

Free Talk

Random Musings 268

— Hua Suo

A person skilled in governing the country and bringing peace to the world can truly see methods for doing so everywhere. In Sichuan, some people believe that long gowns waste cloth and send teams to cut them off; in Shanghai, a public figure wants to regulate teahouses. It is said that there will be three main points of regulation: first, attention to hygiene; second, setting time limits; and third, implementing education.

The first point is certainly good. The second point, where going to a teahouse and hearing a bell like in school is a bit of a hassle, but for the sake of drinking tea, there's no way around it and it's not too bad.

The most difficult is the third point. The 'ignorant masses' come to teahouses not only to hear news and chat, but also to listen to stories like 'The Case of Judge Bao'. The era is long past, and the truth is hard to know, so they listen to nonsense and stay there. If it is changed to 'The Case of Official So-and-So', people might not believe it or want to listen. If you only talk about the secret histories and dark sides of the enemy, what one side calls the enemy might not be the enemy of those listening. So they might not want to listen too earnestly. The result would be that the teahouse owner suffers and business becomes slow.

In the early years of the Guangxu era of the Qing Dynasty, there was an opera troupe in my hometown called 'The Gathering Jade Troupe'. However, the name did not match the reality, and the opera was so bad that no one wanted to watch it. The townsfolk, no less skilled than the great writers, wrote a song for them:

'On stage, the Gathering Jade Troupe,

Below, everyone scatters.

They hastily close the temple door,

Both sides of the wall collapse (flat tone).

They hastily try to hold it up,

Leaving only a noodle vendor.'

The choices of the audience cannot be forced. If they don't want to watch, there is no use in dragging them. Similarly, there are some publications with money and power that could be popular throughout the world. However, not only is the audience limited, but even submissions are few and far between, so they can only publish every two months. Satire is the old man's dream talk of the previous century, and good non-satirical literature seems to be the product of the youth of the next century.

Prostitution Ban 269

— Cao Ju Ren

The issue of whether or not to lift the prostitution ban in Nanjing has been discussed by the Executive Yuan, which shows the importance of the issue. The stated reason for lifting the ban is to alleviate the sluggishness of the market, i.e., to use brothels to boost the economy. The reasons against lifting the ban are mostly focused on morals and ethics, and also mention the dignity of women, etc. It is very difficult to resolve this issue where morality and prosperity cannot be reconciled.

Before the prostitution ban issue is resolved, I would not dare to participate in the discussion. However, after reading the sages' books for many years, I have never known that lifting the prostitution ban would boost the economy, or that not lifting it would maintain morality. The relationship is so significant that I am truly ignorant! However, what I am reminded of is that there was a professor in Beijing who was keen to study social problems. He specially asked a friend to introduce him to a prostitute for an open and honest conversation. The professor asked her, 'Would you like me to help you get out of this?' The professor expected her response to be, if not grateful, at least willing. Who knew that the prostitute would give a negative answer. The prostitute asked the professor, 'If you help me out, what will I do? What can I do? I have an elderly mother and father, three younger brothers, and a younger sister. What will happen to this family?' The professor was speechless and could not answer. (See the Social Problems Biweekly of the Dagong Daily for details.) According to the prostitute's eloquent argument, whether prostitution is banned or not has nothing to do with the prosperity or decline of the market, or the maintenance or loss of morality. She has to eat, her family has to eat, so she has to sell her body. Even a university professor who studies social problems has nothing to say. As the German Karl Kautsky said, 'Capitalists not only take advantage of their inexperience to give them wages that are too low to cover their own expenses, but also imply, or even explicitly say, that prostitution is the only way to supplement their income. Under the capitalist system, prostitution has become a pillar of society.' These words hit the nail on the head.

Stone Statues 270

— Wang Renshu

In the suburbs, among the weeds and rubble, I saw several pairs of imposing stone statues standing tall.

Holding court tablets in their hands and wearing swords at their waists,

each faced the other with a solemn expression.

Months, two months, countless months passed. Years, decades, hundreds of years passed. They battled the storms and raging winds, the thick frost and scorching sun. They endured the chopping of woodcutters and the grazing of shepherds, the nesting of orioles, swallows, crows, and sparrows. They always stood coldly among the weeds and rubble with solemn faces, indifferent to gain and loss, life and death, devoid of love, hatred, bitterness, and joy.

I felt melancholic.

The morning sun shone silently upon their heads.

I turned and moved forward. A red wall was in sight, the front gate of the Ming Xiaoling Mausoleum.

I entered with a sense of reverence. Flowers and trees lined the path, casting shadows. I passed through the memorial hall and arrived at the tomb. In the arched tunnel, I climbed the steps.

On the circular earthen mound, dense old trees grew lushly. The Ming tomb unfolded before my eyes. Serene, ancient, majestic, solemn...

I recalled Zhu Yuanzhang's revolutionary achievements, and I also lamented the surrender of the peasant leader.

On the sandy soil without industrial revolution, the feudal construction of history suppressed the rebellious hearts of all traitors.

I vaguely saw that peasant leader with a resolute will and a face covered in soil, who had seized power with the strength of a sickle. However, he had turned around and discarded the sickle, using the feudal pen to consolidate his own power.

I walked out of the Xiaoling Mausoleum with a sense of despondency. I repeatedly saw those pairs of stone statues, standing coldly among the weeds and rubble.

The morning sun had kissed their entire bodies.

Equipped with the attire and demeanor of scholar-officials, they were like living people in every way. Yet, they had to remain the same for thousands of years, clasping their hands, straightening their waists, and standing tall with solemn faces, indifferent to life and death, gain and loss, devoid of love, hatred, bitterness, and joy, to decorate the... to decorate the majesty of that 'feudal construction'!

I felt melancholic.

Under the morning sun, I walked past those pairs of stone statues, and when my own thin shadow was submerged in their inverted images, I felt a suffocating, melancholic feeling for the similarity of our fates.

On the Use of Gongs and Drums in Old Opera 271

— He Ru

George Bernard Shaw asked Dr. Mei Lanfang, 'Why does Chinese opera need to use gongs and drums?' Dr. Mei replied, 'Some Kunqu operas do not use gongs and drums.' Although this is a quick answer, it is still somewhat evasive. Mr. Ye Gongchuo asked Shaw, 'Why don't you eat meat?' Shaw said, 'I don't eat meat because I don't eat meat.' Dr. Mei should have answered Shaw, 'Chinese opera needs gongs and drums because Chinese opera needs gongs and drums.' Responding with humor is a matter of etiquette, and wouldn't this further demonstrate that China is a land of ritual and should not be underestimated? Shaw has no respect for China, and I can retort with 'Don't say Qin has no men!' Previously, I saw Mr. Ju Ren's article on gongs and drums in Free Talk, which sparked my thoughts and I intended to elaborate, but I was unable to do so due to being confined to bed by illness. Now Dr. Mei has come to Shanghai again to perform his skills, and the sound of gongs and drums fills the ears, how can I remain silent?

I believe that as long as there is Chinese opera, it cannot be separated from gongs and drums, whether it is considered a national dross or a national treasure depends on individual wisdom and opinion. The Huabu Luan Tan operas certainly cannot avoid the noise of gongs and drums. Even Kunqu opera values gongs and drums. In the early Qing Dynasty, Li Yu had already spoken of avoiding excessive gongs and drums. He believed that the gongs and drums in the opera were related to the tendons and joints. Striking when one should not, not striking when one should, emphasizing when one should be light, and lightening when one should be heavy, all detract from the value of the opera. There is great truth in this, which only those who are experienced in opera know. The worst thing is to suddenly interrupt at a crucial moment, such as when the spoken dialogue is not finished, or when the melody is just beginning, with indiscriminate striking that covers the sound, causing the listener to miss a few sentences and fail to understand the connection between events, or causing the auditor not to hear the starting note and not know what song will be sung later. Interrupting the song is forgivable, but obscuring the dialogue is inexcusable. There is also the case where an opera is about to end, with only a few lines of dialogue left, and these few lines are the key, but the gongs and drums of the opera house are already urging the end, making the saying or not saying the same, which is regrettable. Therefore, the speed and emphasis must be carefully considered. If those on stage will not speak, then the blame cannot be placed solely on the actor, but the gongs and drums are equally at fault. Li Yu's argument was made during the decline of Kunqu opera, and no one paid attention at the time. When Luan Tan arose, the gongs and drums became even more disordered, and this was considered necessary to make the scene lively, which is why Luan Tan is called Luan Tan. The so-called Luan Tan now takes Erhuang as the orthodox style. The instruments used in Erhuang, such as large gongs, small gongs, small cymbals, large drums, large cymbals, small cymbals, and clappers, can only produce irregular noise. They either add to the liveliness of the scene, determine the beginning and end of the recitation, express the tension and relaxation of emotions, or indicate the speed of actions. The function of gongs and drums is such, but its musical significance is not worth mentioning. The way of striking gongs and drums, apart from the "paizi" tunes, can be divided into about twenty kinds. The "shui long yin" and "jiang jun ling" among the "paizi" tunes seem to be a kind of harmony organization, but in fact they are only used to control the rhythm and enhance the momentum. In the Erhuang of the past twenty years, the louder the gongs and drums, the better. In martial arts operas, they do not hesitate to break the large gong to enhance the prestige of the characters. Mr. Ouyang Yuqian said that the ears of such drummers are more developed than ordinary people, and some even become deaf in old age. Although this sounds like a joke, it is actually the case.

In short, I believe that the distant origins of Chinese opera come from wrestling. The wrestling performances of the Qin, Han, Sui, and Tang Dynasties were also called San Yue, which can be found in the chronicles and musical annals. Martial arts require gongs and drums to indicate advance and retreat and to strengthen the array, and music cannot do without metal and leather instruments. Is this why old Chinese opera does not abandon martial arts and gongs and drums? I wonder what Dr. Mei thinks.

Carrot Whiskers 272

— Written by Julos Kenaro, Translated by Lin Qu

Silver Coin

III (Continued)

Carrot Whiskers, who had already walked away, turned around when he heard these words and took a few steps behind his mother. Finally, he suddenly rushed in front of his mother, blocked the way, and silently presented his face.

The Lepic's (raising his right hand to strike down)! I know you lie, but I didn't expect you to be so cunning. Now, you've told two lies. If this continues, you'll start by stealing an egg, then steal a cow, and then you'll murder his mother. (The first slap landed)

Personal Thoughts

Mr. Lepic, elder brother Felix, elder sister Elestine, and Carrot Whiskers were chatting in front of the fireplace after dinner. A tree root was burning in the fireplace, and all four chairs were rocking on their front two legs. Everyone was arguing, and Carrot Whiskers was expressing his personal thoughts when the Lepic's weren't around.

'In my opinion,' he said, 'family titles mean nothing. For example, Dad, you know how much I love you! But I love you not because you are my father, but because you are my friend. In fact, you have done nothing to deserve being my father, but I consider your friendship towards me a high favor, a favor you could have chosen not to give me, but you generously gave it to me.'

'Ah!' Lepic replied.

'What about me? What about me?' elder brother Felix and elder sister Elestine asked together.

'It's the same,' Carrot Whiskers said. 'Fate made you my brother and sister. Why should I thank you for that? If the three of us had not been born into the Lepic family, who is to blame? You were powerless to prevent this from happening. I don't need to feel happy about this kind of familial relationship that doesn't come from the heart. All I need to thank you for is that, brother, you protect me, and sister, you give me useful care.'

'It's our duty to serve you,' elder brother Felix said.

'Why does he have to think of such ideas?' elder sister Elestine said.

'And what I've said, I can summarize and affirm. I'm not referring to anyone in particular, and even if Mom were here, I would repeat it to her face.'

'You wouldn't repeat it twice,' elder brother Felix said.

'What's wrong with what I said?' Carrot Whiskers replied. 'Please don't change my mind! I'm not only not a heartless person, but the love I have for you is even deeper than what's on the surface. But this kind of love is not mundane, instinctive, habitual, but intentional, rational, and logical. Logical, yes, that's the word I'm looking for.'

'When are you going to break this habit?!! This habit of liking to use words that you don't even understand yourself and then trying to teach them to others before they're even dry behind the ears,' Lepic said, as he stood up to go to bed. 'If your grandfather were alive, he would have given me a kick or a slap the moment he heard a quarter of what you said, to prove that I was still his child.' (To be continued)

Small Talk

Farewell to a Giant Turtle 273

— Xiao Zhi

Recently, though my mouth itched, I kept silent for quite some time because a dog-skin plaster was stuck on it, making it inconvenient to speak. Yesterday, while leafing through a certain newspaper, I thought that national affairs were beyond the comprehension of us children, and I was too lazy to worry about them. So, I diligently read news items like "Human Desires Run Rampant: Thirteen or Fourteen-Year-Old Boys and Girls Truly Ensnared," "Robbery of 128,000 Yuan in Cash," and "Red Pills," "Poisons," etc., one by one with great interest. Finally, I stumbled upon something strange and wonderful, so wonderful that it made my stomach hurt from laughing!

This incident happened in Changshu. The newspaper reported it as follows:

A fisherman caught a giant turtle "with a head the size of a bamboo dustpan, feet like wings without claws, and dozens of white plum-like spots on its back, measuring seven feet long and weighing hundreds of pounds." He transported it into the city for exhibition in the park. When this was known to benevolent people, they all considered the turtle to possess spiritual power and advocated for its release. Therefore, they collected 350 yuan to buy it from the fisherman. Yesterday, these great benefactors, along with the abbot of a certain temple, escorted the turtle with firecrackers and military music from the park to outside the Great Eastern Gate, where it boarded a pre-arranged gasoline boat to be released directly into the Hu River...

Reading this, I was greatly surprised. What surprised me was that "such a large turtle could actually exist in this world, and that such a large turtle was worthy of being seen off with 'firecrackers and military music' by the so-called benefactors." However, regarding the "farewell," in today's world where we are accustomed to "farewells," this is not surprising, let alone a farewell to a giant turtle, a spiritually powerful turtle.

As for what I call strange and wonderful, so wonderful that it makes my stomach hurt from laughing, and worth writing about in detail, it's all here:

...The boat had two armed guards with box cannons fore and aft for protection. (Xiao Zhi thinks this was probably to prevent kidnapping or assassination?) When passing Meili, tens of thousands of people crowded the shore, eager to see what was happening. (Xiao Zhi asks, was the scene more grand than the Human Sea that gathered at Taihe Hall in Beijing last October 21 to see the Panchen Lama's Dharma image for the Kalachakra Dharma Assembly?)… The only "Zhenyu" warship stationed in the Hu River, which protected the people from bandits in Changshu, had already lit its fires and was waiting to depart. All the officers and men of the warship stood at attention. Upon seeing the gasoline boat with the turtle, they immediately carried the turtle onto the warship. The escorting party also boarded the warship, and the warship immediately sailed at full speed to a point thirty li outside the river mouth. The police officers then carried the turtle down into the water. At that time, the abbot led the party in chanting release mantras, (Xiao Zhi shouts Amitabha Buddha, Namo Avalokiteśvara Bodhisattva,) kneeling and respectfully sending it off. The ceremony was extremely grand. (Xiao Zhi says, it should be so, otherwise, if the giant turtle got angry or caused trouble, wouldn't the common people suffer?) After the turtle had left, the warship began to return, and the escorting party also took the original boat back to the city. (Hard work, escorting party!)

Xiao Zhi's required calculation is that in this event, besides the giant turtle being free to be reborn and gloriously return to its watery home, and a certain fisherman getting 350 yuan to go home and have a feast, (1) the people of Changshu were exhausted, (2) the police were sweating profusely (the police were the great heroes who released the turtle into the water), (3) a certain amount of firecrackers were set off, a certain amount of gasoline and "ship coal" were burned, in addition to armed guards, military music, chanting, kneeling...

Xiao Zhi then laughed and cried, from pain to sorrow.

Literature & Art

Sentiments 274

— Jin Zhi

Leaning on the tower, composing poems to the wind and moon, what do national affairs have to do with strategizing? How many people can sit in command like Ma Sui?

Petitioning for justice echoes Han Xiu's memorials. Looking up at Wu and Gui, I reminisce about the past; turning back to Hangzhou, I regret former travels. The surging waters of the Pu River flow westward, as a student, I harbor Jia Yi's worries. Living in the countryside, it's difficult to avoid becoming a recluse; today, I remain in the aftermath of chaos. Is it possible to relight the Ge Hong's furnace? How many Fan Li's pots remain from half a lifetime? Flying ducks can still be seen after a thousand years, while taming cranes once spread a feather and are lost. The vicissitudes of the world increase my emotions, and I still discuss pacifying the people with the Tianbao era as an example.

Lingering Echoes 275

— Bin Fu

Let's not talk about national affairs; let me talk about romance. "Romance"? The weather is right in the middle of the plum rain season, and the wind makes people feel unhappy; the moon? The moon is also at the end of its period, although after ten o'clock it may emerge from the clouds, pitiable... On a night with no wind and no moonlight, I just sit quietly in my room. In the deep silence, I suddenly hear the lingering echoes of Bai Yunpeng and Xiao Hei Guniang's drums.

I only saw Bai Yunpeng and Xiao Hei Guniang a few days before they left. That night, I was feeling very bored, so I decided to take a stroll in the Beiping book market. Although I don't understand drums very well, I can appreciate the leisurely charm of them. It was still early when I got to the book market, and there were other people singing. Through the singing of these people, I gained a better understanding of the true essence of drums. Later, Xiao Hei Guniang came out gracefully from behind the curtain amidst the cheers of the audience. She was truly a beautiful girl. In the midst of the flowers and lights on the stage, she looked even more charming. These flowers were all gifts from affectionate young gentlemen, as a farewell souvenir. I remember that night, there were two comedians interspersing their performance by saying:

"Who are you going to give these flowers to?" "These are all for our Xiao Hei Guniang." "Why are you giving her flowers?" "This is a sign of affection from the young masters who are in love with the girl. Later, these flowers may be returned to them." "Why is that?" "Because when the young masters think of the girl after she leaves, they can smell them, and it will be like seeing the girl." I found this very interesting.

Xiao Hei Guniang sang "The Great Western Chamber" that day, and she sang it with great ups and downs. When she sang the line "Lonely, lonely, cold, clear, empty, laborious, desolate, cool...", it was like the galloping of rain in an empty mountain. But when she sang "Lowering her head, silent, speechless, her waist is thin...", it was like the pauses and breaks in the secluded warbling of an oriole. But in the second half, the cheers grew louder and louder, but her voice was drowned out. Soon, Xiao Hei Guniang went inside. I drank a cup of tea and waited for Bai Yunpeng. I imagined that this northerner must be a burly man, but to my surprise, a refined scholar with an elegant demeanor came out, which was really beyond my expectations! He was probably over fifty years old, and he spoke very fluent Beipinghua, and every word was very clear. He had rich emotions, and he had a humble attitude. Because that night was the last day, he said a lot of things: "...Goodbye, everyone, finally goodbye. We, these humble and insignificant trifles, are very grateful and ashamed to have gained your appreciation. Although we have put a lot of effort into our art, we are still just wandering beggars..." How tactful and emotional these words are. He was singing "Daiyu Burning Manuscripts." He said, "...These days, I have been singing the Dream of the Red Chamber. The Dream of the Red Chamber is naturally a very good material, but it has made me suffer. Every day I sing a section, I always have to cry for a while!..." Listen, how poetic these words are! His singing was most satisfying to me. Quick and slow, every word conveyed the spirit. When he sang quickly, it was like a shower; when he sang softly, it was like weeping. In particular, the section "...Her slender willow waist can't be held in one hand, her apricot face is yellowed from illness, her oriole voice is hoarse from constant coughing, her delicate breath can't stop her pink nose from flaring..." was especially moving to me; when he sang "...Who is like me, lonely and bitter, even more sad...", his eyes were moist. This was a very deep impression for me.

Bai Yunpeng's art is worthy of praise. He gave me a deep impression. But they left. Every time I rest after work, I miss this artist. I can only 空地 appreciate 腦 的 的 lingering echoes.

At the Table 276

— Huan Yi

The weekly dinner party; this is already the fourth time. Judging from the past three times, it has generally been smooth. However, although it is limited to one small cup of wine per person, at the end of each dinner, there are always one or two people whose faces are as red as a rising fire, at least somewhat unsteady. But, clearly, this is not drunkenness.

Around a lavish twelve-dollar feast, ten foodies were gathered, men and women mixed together, of course, with no distinction between guests and hosts. Each person was full of energy, displaying their daily practiced skills. Dishes came up, orders were given, and chopsticks rained down on the same plate, until the bottom of the plate was completely exposed.

Aimless small talk, from all over the country to all over the world, but trying to find the beginning of the first sentence is often impossible to trace. We don't know what we started talking about, but we talked about prostitutes and dancers.

"Prostitutes and dancers, they all willingly fell." So, Mrs. Li expressed some opinions on them. "A person, given two hands by nature, can do anything. Why must they do such a base thing?"

"That's right! They..." Miss Wang echoed her with sympathy.

"However, it's not just the woman's fault." Mrs. Li suddenly changed the subject, seemingly showing some forgiveness towards prostitutes and dancers. "If there were no men to mess around, how could they gain a foothold? So, it's still the men's fault." Of course, Mrs. Li was not shooting without a target.

Mr. Li silently ate his melon seeds.

"That's not necessarily true! It's also because life forces them to be like this." Da Ge probably saw Mr. Li's cramped and uneasy attitude, which was too embarrassing, so he was the first to raise an objection. But he was, after all, a kind and honest elder, so his words were always relatively peaceful. But the debate started at this time.

"Then, Mr. Lin... They are oppressed by life, which is pitiful, so please take care of them!" You don't have to hear what Xiao Zhang said, you can know his personality just by seeing his face. Especially today, in front of Miss Wang, he naturally stood on her side of the battle line and particularly showed his sharp skills. Then there was a cold laugh that didn't move his face or flesh.

Mrs. Li and Miss Wang laughed triumphantly, and everyone laughed. Da Ge was a little embarrassed, and he pretended to be calm, aiming at the plate and eating the dish. At this time, suddenly, a new force rushed out from my side and joined the opposition with determination, saying...

"Everyone must know... this issue... is not just a matter of a few people, nor is it solely the responsibility of men. Who should be responsible for some of it? In other words, an attack by an environment in life cannot be resisted by an individual; the entire society should be responsible for it." Mr. Ye's face was completely red, and in his neck, there was a green vein as thick as a finger. Finally, he muttered to himself... "Who doesn't want to eat a twelve-dollar feast?"

At that time, there were obviously two opposing factions. The remaining four people also joined the battle line based on their own positions. As a result, in a not-so-large room, the air suddenly became tense, and a round table with messy dishes was used as the battlefield for a great debate.

Shop Employees' Correspondence

A Worker's Frustration 277

Editor:

I am a worker, so my knowledge is lacking. When I encounter problems, I always have difficulties. Now I have encountered a problem again. Please take some time to instruct me, and I will never forget your kindness.

I have a friend who used to be an apprentice in a cigarette paper shop not far from my home, so I knew him. Later, he became a trainee at a certain hospital. As for me, I still do this work like a horse in a factory. After the "January 28th" incident last year, I lost my job. Later, he helped me find a job as a trainee at a certain pharmacy, but it required 100 yuan for room and board, and it took a year to graduate. Later, I realized that this pharmacy was cunning, recruiting trainees as a trick to earn 100 yuan. Therefore, I did not fall into this trap. But my friend, he looked down on me for it, saying that I had no aspirations and was taking a path of decline. Later, I found a job in another factory. This was last year. Recently, I ran into that friend again. He still said in that tone that working in a factory will never allow you to turn over. I was really pissed off by his words. Later, I thought to myself that his words were not wrong. I am determined to work hard and make progress in this industrial field. Our industry is lacquer manufacturing. Although I can't talk about academic qualifications in this industry now, I do have some achievements in practical experience. However, even with achievements, you must have knowledge and assets to control them. Therefore, my success in this industry is like waiting for a day with no sun. I want to improve my knowledge, but my monthly income is only 13 yuan. Food, clothing, and shelter are all paid for here, and if I am sick and take leave, my salary will be deducted. Therefore, it is very difficult to satisfy my desire for knowledge. I don't know if there are any free schools anywhere. If there are any kind-hearted gentlemen who can lead me out of this situation, that would be a great favor to me. I want to ask, is there any hope for me to satisfy my desire for knowledge in this way in the future? Finally, my father often asks me for money. It's not that I'm unwilling, but the truth is that I don't have any extra money to give to my father! Please also help me think of a way! Wishing you

Well-being, Shen Xiaoqin

XXXX Editor's Note: Society is supported by the joint efforts of all parties, so if a person, in addition to sitting and eating, can do commensurate work to offset his consumption, then there is no distinction between noble and lowly: being an official and being a "beggar," both are serving the community. Understanding this principle, we can achieve the level of "constancy" and not be fickle, which leads to no results. Your friend's words, although spoken out of enthusiasm, are inevitably somewhat prejudiced against laborers: it is best to explain your position to him tactfully, otherwise, "thank you for your concern" will also do. It is right for you to be determined to make progress in the industrial field; as for the duties in the pharmacy, because it is not something you are familiar with, even if it is not cunning, there is nothing to regret.

As for completely free supplementary schools that suit you, we have not heard of any; this is entirely because they also have their own expenses. However, there are many places in Shanghai that charge very low fees and can reduce them for the poor. You can ask the supplementary schools near your residence to reduce the fees. Unfortunately, the several amateur supplementary schools currently run by this newspaper are too far from your place; if you don't mind being a little further away, or if we add new ones in the future, we can make special arrangements.

Between father and son, there is a matter of nature; if you are very embarrassed, just be sincere with him, and perhaps he will not want to make things difficult for you. But if his difficulties are far greater than yours, then you should also give a little bit. In short, it should depend on your ability and his needs, and be open and honest.

Fiction

Under the Traffic Lights (7) 278

— Xi Lin

After a while, Shi Qiao walked back from the east again, unexpectedly and boldly grabbed her hand, and then went upstairs to his room without saying anything.

Meizi followed him into his room involuntarily, and couldn't find the right words, so she asked, "What are you doing back here? Don't you look very busy?"

"We are going to fight with you too, do you know? I came back to write a plan for how we will organize student volunteers, and they will go and make connections separately!"

"What? You are going to fight with us? Aren't we good friends who have been together for a long time, and aren't we still living together?"

Shi Qiao smiled and couldn't answer. From Meizi's question, it became clear that the so-called national hatred was not among the general populace, and that the Japanese imperialist invasion of China was not for the populace. How disconnected this was from Meizi! The enemies Shi Qiao was going to fight were certainly not Meizi's, but Meizi's "them"!

After this very natural question, Meizi was inexplicably touched by the sadness of her floating existence. Her eyelids drooped, and her hands lightly twisted her clothing buttons. Li Shi Qiao knew that he had misspoke, and always wanted to say a few words to comfort her, but the more anxious he was, the less he could find the right gentle words, just staring at her blankly: looking at this foreign, fallen girl, with her plain clothes! She never wears Japanese clothes! Combined with her thin and slender figure, the cold feeling was like a Western nun; that "beauty" moves people with the light of a spiritual soul. Shi Qiao initially stretched out his hands, making a posture of almost wanting to hug her, but then retracted his hands! It is not okay to hug a married woman, and it is not okay to bully a pitiful woman; but that hand twisting the clothing button hooked his arm, and that body came even closer, and her powerless head leaned on his shoulder, and gentle words slowly leaked from her pale lips;

"Are you really going to fight? Mr. Li!" Pausing, "War, war, why is there war?"

Movie Special

Before Greta Garbo Returned to Hollywood 279

— Xun Nan

Where can one entrust the sorrow of parting? The scenery of the old palace still lingers for a few days. Greta Garbo has already returned to Hollywood. After so much confusion, the enigma has finally been broken. On March 24th, she boarded a ship very secretly and quietly left Gothenburg, Sweden. After five weeks at sea, she safely arrived at San Diego, California, USA, on April 30th. An American film magazine, ScreenBook, recorded her activities in great detail. The following are some of Greta Garbo's deeds before leaving Sweden, because this small chronicle can reveal some poignant emotions in the midst of extreme ordinariness, so it has been translated.

Greta Garbo bid farewell to the capital of Sweden. She and her friend Max Gumpel drove around the streets in his Duesenberg car for a week. Gumpel is an engineer whom Garbo knew before she went to Hollywood. This time Garbo returned to her hometown, and Gumpel was her companion, accompanying her in tennis, swimming, and dancing. Because of his advocacy, she invested a considerable amount of capital in real estate in Stockholm, and she has bought at least two houses. She and he toured all over Stockholm, lingering and reluctant to leave, probably because the grass and trees of her hometown would surely haunt her dreams after she left. A week before she left Stockholm, Garbo and her old friends Count Gösta Ekman and Countess Ekman went to see the premiere of the film "Grand Hotel." Because it was a film starring her, she was persuaded to appear in front of the screen.

On March 14th, news spread that Miss Garbo had booked a cabin on the ship Gripsholm, scheduled to set sail on April 1st. So, the general reporters were very busy preparing. But Garbo was also too mischievous, because April 1st is April Fool's Day, so the reporters only understood after being fooled.

On March 21st, Ms. Garbo left her residence at 7 Dottninggatan and made a final visit to her mother and brothers, and then went to a別 with each one individually. It was not until that evening that she was found in Tyersö, which is Count Wrangel's villa and also Garbo's paradise for escaping people. That crack is about fifty miles away from Stockholm and is a place with secluded scenery. This villa was originally a palace built in 1630, but at the end of the 17th century, it fell into the hands of the Wrangel family. On the 22nd and 23rd, Garbo wandered and lingered in this place, quietly entrusting her sorrow of parting to various places. Sometimes she rode with Jonniella Wrangel, the daughter of Wrangel, and went out to play, without any sign of saying goodbye to her hometown. But on Friday, the 24th, the Wrangel couple left Tyersö for Gothenburg. They boarded the ship, with an unknown person in between. The ship was named Annie Johnson, and the strange guest was named Mr. John EmerSon. The captain specially built a swimming pool and other luxurious facilities for this strange guest. After the strange guest boarded the ship, the captain immediately summoned all the crew to meet and instructed them not to mention the name of this strange guest. But a nurse who heard that she was assigned to wait on this strange guest was so happy that she almost fainted!

Film Review of "Madchen in Uniform" (Girls in Uniform) 280

— Ling He

New Style, Good Technique

丨A Miniature of Society in Turmoil丨

Indeed, this is a rare gem among European and American films. If we can objectively let go of excessive strictness or unrealistic expectations, we can acknowledge that this is the highest achievement possible within capitalist cinema. To go further in expression, only Soviet works dare to be so bold.

The film's plot centers on the emotional conflict between female students and their headmistress. Innocent and peaceful girls yearning for freedom, craving genuine love between people. However, the feudal

headmistress subjects them to militaristic education, forbidding all their freedom. This causes internal resentment among the students. Although usually subdued under oppressive forces, they are ultimately moved by collective sympathy, bordering on unrest. In the end, the headmistress realizes her management has failed and voluntarily resigns.

On the surface, the film's primary purpose seems to be opposing militaristic education. In reality, the clever filmmakers use the film as a microcosm of a society in turmoil, illustrating the conflict between the oppressors and the oppressed. The majority of people are starving for benevolence and peace, sacrificing for freedom, wanting to breathe and live in the air of freedom. Yet, the oppressors do not grant them the opportunity for freedom, offering at best only a limited scope of joy during occasions like "the headmistress's birthday, a school gathering to celebrate." It is evident that the oppressors, with their supreme authority, attempt to preserve

their rule forever, even resorting to driving people to their deaths. However, this opposition of "love and hate" will one day erupt in a total explosion, and to avoid this unfortunate destruction, the only way is to request that the rulers voluntarily relinquish their rule! This is the greatest concern of the film's author.

Of course, this is the most thorough solution for those standing in the position of the oppressor who fear hearing the cries of the oppressed. Because they understand the physical principle that "the higher the pressure, the higher the resistance," it is better to relinquish the position of oppressor rather than wait for a future explosion that cannot be controlled. But is it truly unnecessary for the water's resistance to make the cork come loose on its own? This, of course, is a non-physical fantasy. Furthermore, the headmistress leaving the school is merely to have a female teacher replace her with a more lenient and moderate management style. It's not as though the school will be run by the students themselves. Therefore, the film does not abandon its own position, but merely believes that this form is not very reasonable. Regarding the performance, it is not only novel because it is entirely female, but also because it has a clear new style. Not exaggerated, not old-fashioned, not dull, not nonsensical. On the contrary, it is authentic, vivid, calm, and compact. It completely abandons the old ways of typical European and American films, and strives to create a new tone. For example, the dance scene is not about extravagance but about the pressure of emotions. The female students' bathing scene is merely a sketch of school life, not a display of sensuality. There is humor, but not nonsense. The depiction of oppressive forces is thorough and detailed, especially the sound of the headmistress's leather shoes, truly a subtle and insightful portrayal. In short, for a female writer-turned-director to achieve such results in her directorial debut, Leontine Sagan, is truly admirable. However, the final scene where everyone shouts M2nuela (a student's name) to such a weak ending is somewhat regrettable.

As for the group of actors, they are all important and all willing to perform seriously, without exaggeration or laziness, which is also commendable. That crowd scenes can be so well done also shows the director's skillful technique. The female teacher's performance with tears welling up in her eyes is naturally a perfectly executed technique. However, due to limited space, other aspects will be omitted.

Review of "The Road to Physical Fitness I" 281

— Yan Nan

This empty script tells us the astonishing (?) story of a female street performer who falls in love with a wealthy young man. The wealthy young man, for her sake,

breaks off his engagement with his original fiancée, achieving the goal of marriage. The wealthy young man even joins the street performance troupe to perform.

But the film's performance! Is a thousand times more complex than what is written above. It unintentionally depicts the past history of the female street performer, even including the affairs of three generations of ancestors, taking up over a thousand feet of film. Although it is

reflecting their courage and indomitable spirit, it is ultimately a waste. Of course, there are also many legitimate narratives in the script, such as writing about the hardships of street performing life, the audience's unforgiving nature, and the world's emphasis on beauty over artistry. These are relatively realistic sketches that can evoke sympathy. However, these are fragmented and trivial, flaws outweighing the merits, making it difficult to give a good impression. There are also many extremely boring actions, such as the public invitation to perform at the end, which is certainly embarrassing for the parties involved, but is it ultimately an insult? And is it worth it to be motivated to go back to street performing because of this? In short, distorted consciousness abounds. With a better script intention, but unable to fully develop it, and adding disjointed and chaotic semi-new ideas, the entire script loses its focus. In particular, the film's grand finale, taking "going back to street performing" as the only bright path on the "Road to Physical Fitness," is even more puzzling! The great performance at the end promoting sports and enlightening the public is also not seen in the film! (It is in the explanatory pamphlet). The director is relatively good, but the script is too long, with many flashbacks and repetitions. Over ten thousand feet of film is simply not enough, so places where it could be developed are all omitted. The director used a lot of ingenuity in the small places, so the structure is very commendable. The cleverness of the scene divisions is indeed above "Peace Flower," with appropriate side descriptions and comparisons.

The cinematography can also be considered competent, diligently helping the director to complete the work. Although the forward and backward movements and transitions are inevitably stiff, the angles of the fixed position shots are well coordinated. The long shots and outdoor shots are relatively worse. The light is too weak, which is not very suitable for this "degenerate martial arts film," so it increases the "beauty" of the picture but reduces the "strength" of the film. The set design for the street performance venues is somewhat unrealistic, and the wealth and extravagance of the wealthy family seem excessive.

The sentences in the subtitles are both profound and as emotional as new poetry, so many people cannot understand them. Even if they do understand, they will feel that they are not related to the performance in the film.

Finally, it is time to talk about the performance. We already know that this film is "semi-martial arts," and street performances account for one-third of it. Adding that the film is so long, there is simply no opportunity to consider the development of the performance, it is just everyone playing a certain person and acting. However, I cannot help but say a few words about the main characters. The female street performer is Xu Qin Fang, who has always only known martial arts and not literature. Although she plays three roles (her grandmother and her mother), she only does fighting besides high jumping and tightrope walking. Her martial arts skills are not bad. Zheng Xiao Qiu plays the wealthy young man, with an excess of weakness and extravagance, and not enough steadfastness and depth. "He is a good son in the eyes of the old lady, but not a youth of the times," someone said, and it seems like a very fitting comment. His expression is only ordinary, and indeed, he is better in the first half as a handsome young man, but he seems very strained in the second half. Yan Gong Shang plays the wealthy old man, experienced and calm, fitting the identity of a conservative wealthy man. Xie Yun Qing, the head of the street performance troupe, is too literary, not like someone who travels the world, groaning and turning, sickly and fragmented, but very brilliant, indeed an actor with pure skill. Gao Yi An (wife of the wealthy man) and Xu Xin Yuan (the bully) are also only勉强 acting.

Cinema Novel Reunited in Vienna (9) 282

— Translated by Zi Gui

Rudolf and Barolomo rushed out, hailed a streetcar, and unceremoniously drove the conductor to the back car. Rudolf sat in the conductor's seat and drove the car himself. But when Rudolf got into the car, his greatcoat got caught on the car

door. Rudolf forcefully threw his greatcoat over his shoulder, revealing the shining white uniform inside. The two policemen standing at the door saw this, nodded knowingly, and blew their whistles. At this time, the car had shot out like an arrow. At Andenkrug's house, the doorbell suddenly rang continuously. Elena had already returned a few minutes ago, wearing a military greatcoat on the outside, and she didn't know where her own coat had gone. After she came back, she said goodnight to Anden and went back to her bedroom to sleep. Her complexion was very bad. Anden was thinking to himself at this time, had his plan been messed up, but the maid had already opened the door. Rudolf and Barolomo rushed in like madmen.

"Are you a doctor?" Rudolf asked.

"Yes," Anden nodded. They looked at each other for a while, and Rudolf said...

"So you are the Doctor Professor. I really find it a bit strange. I always thought you were a long-bearded old man. Pleased to meet you." After he finished speaking, he bowed respectfully.

"Who are you?" Anden asked. Rudolf took a few steps back in surprise, and Barolomo quickly introduced him. Rudolf said he wanted to see Elena. Anden replied that she had already gone to sleep. Rudolf said it didn't matter, he could call her up. Anden looked at him, then sent someone to call Elena. At this time, Rudolf sent Barolomo away, and Anden said to Rudolf, "I very

like to see you."

"You like to see me?" Rudolf stammered a little.

"You probably can also imagine why I like to see you. You seem to have existed in our house for a long time, ever since the day I married Elena. Of course, I can tell you that this is not a welcome thing, but I have no way to drive you away, as if this house is occupied by you. Now when I see you, I think you are not such a terrible thing." "Oh," Rudolf said hesitantly, "I have met many women's husbands, but you are the first to tell me lies. I also like to meet you, you are truly a doctor worthy of the name." After he finished speaking, he ran over and stretched out his hand to shake Anden's. Elena was now upstairs looking down. Anden told her that they had become friends. Elena responded and came downstairs. Rudolf sat in a large chair and said comfortably... (To be continued)

Home
